# M10 Phase 9 — Tier T7 findings — interrogation view

**Cluster:** M10 — Sin, Guilt and Transgression
**Tier:** T7
**Prompts in tier:** 20
**Characteristics:** 22
**Finding blocks below:** 440

Each prompt in this tier is shown in catalogue order. Under each prompt, all 22 characteristics' findings are stacked verbatim. No analytics, no grouping, no synthesis suggestions — just the raw data organised tier-by-tier for open exploration.

Status codes: **E** = evidenced; **S** = silent; **G** = gap.

---

## T7.1 — Lexical and Semantic Analysis

### T7.1.1

**Question:** What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The primary Hebrew term is **cha.ta (H2398)** — a verb whose root meaning is "to miss (a target), to go wrong, to offend, to incur guilt." The root imagery of missing a mark (the physical sense appears in Judg 20:16 — slingers who would not "miss," same root) applied to the moral realm names sin as a *directional failure*: the person aimed elsewhere than the moral mark. The primary NT term is **hamartanō (G0264)** — from hamartia, likewise meaning "to miss, to err, to sin." The semantic convergence of Hebrew and Greek roots around the "missing the mark" image is analytically significant: both Testaments anchor wilful sinning in the concept of a directional failure — not a neutral act but one that misses what was aimed at. Paraptōma (G3900, once in VCG-05: Gal 6:1) means "a false step, a trespass" — accidental entanglement rather than directed missing.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The primary Hebrew construction is **cha.ta (H2398) + bishgagah** — the verb (sin, miss the mark) combined with the adverb derived from the root *shagah* (to err, to wander, to go astray without intending to). The root *shagah* carries the sense of *unintentional wandering from the path* — the person who strays not through rebellion but through inadvertence. Num 15:27 — "ki tekheta bishgagah" — "when he sins in error/inadvertence." The *shagah* root (with its derivatives *shegagah* H7684 — inadvertent sin, and *shegag* H7683 — to err unintentionally) is the vocabulary that specifically names the unintentional quality, absent from CHAR-1's corpus. The VCG-02 cultic-purification use of cha.ta in the Piel stem (to de-sin, purify) does not carry the *bishgagah* qualifier — it is cha.ta as a denominative process-verb rather than an act-of-sinning description.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The primary Hebrew term is **cha.ta (H2398) in its first-person perfect confessional form**: *chatati* ("I have sinned") and *chatanu* ("we have sinned"). The root (miss the mark, offend, incur guilt) applied in the first-person perfect creates the confessional form: the act of sinning (marked by the root) is now named as completed by the speaker themselves. This is not a distinct confession-vocabulary but the sinning-vocabulary deployed self-referentially. A secondary Hebrew term appears in the corpus through the confession-formula: *yadat* (to know) in 2Sa 19:20 — "your servant *knows* that I have sinned" — the cognitive-knowledge basis of confession. The NT primary term is **hamartanō (G0264) in its aorist/perfect self-application**: Mat 27:4 — *hēmarton* ("I sinned"), Luk 15:18/21 — *hēmarton* ("I have sinned"). No dedicated confession-term appears; the sinning vocabulary is self-applied.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The primary Hebrew term is **cha.ta (H2398)** in three forms: (1) the *negated first-person perfect* (Jer 2:35 — "I have not sinned" — *lo chatati*), the direct inversion of the confessional form; (2) the *participle/sinner-type* (Ecc 2:26; 8:12 — "the sinner" — *hachotet/lehachotet*), naming the person constituted by the characteristic; (3) the *question-form* (Jer 16:10 — "what is the sin that we have committed?" — using the noun form alongside the verb). The NT primary terms are **hamartanō (G0264)** in the present continuous (1Cor 15:34 — "do not go on sinning" — ongoing action) and the adjectival/participial **hamartōlos-equivalent** in Tit 3:11 ("sinful"). The root meaning — "to miss the mark" — deployed in the negated/suppressed mode reveals: the characteristic is the refusal to acknowledge what the root reveals — that the mark has been missed.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — No single dedicated Hebrew or Greek term names refusal to repent; the characteristic is expressed through *compound constructions*. The primary OT construction is: **lo sar min** ("did not turn aside from") or **lo sur min** ("did not depart from") + **chat.tat** (the sins of Jeroboam). Sur (H5493) means to turn aside, depart, remove; its negated form (*lo sur*) names the refusal-direction explicitly. The complementary construction is **davaq** (H1692 — 2Ki 3:3: "clung to") meaning to cling, adhere, be joined — revealing the active dimension of the refusal. The OT bodily-metaphor construction is **qashu et-orpam** (Neh 9:29 — "stiffened their neck" — H7185 qasha: to be hard, stiff) + **natan kateph sorerah** ("gave a stubborn shoulder" — H5637 sarar: to be stubborn/rebellious). The primary NT construction is **hekousiōs hamartanontōn** (Heb 10:26: sinning willingly/deliberately) and **hamartanontōn** in the present continuous (1Ti 5:20: those persisting in sin).

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The primary Hebrew term is **cha.ta (H2398)** in three CHAR-6-distinctive configurations: (1) *Person-type participial*: *hachotet* ("the sinner" — Ecc 7:26; 9:2/18; Pro 11:31/13:22) — the participial used as a substantive naming the constituted sinner-type; (2) *Iterative verb*: "sinned yet again" (Exo 9:34) — the verb used with temporal repetition markers; (3) *Pattern-continuation*: "you have sinned... there they have continued" (Hos 10:9) — sinning as an unbroken temporal pattern. The root meaning ("to miss the mark, to incur guilt") deployed in these configurations reveals: habitual defection is the root action (*miss the mark*) stabilised into a person-type and a continuing pattern rather than an episodic act. The NT primary terms are: **hamartanō (G0264)** in the present continuous (*hamartanōn* — 1Jo 3:6: "keeps on sinning") and the constative aorist (*hēmarton* — Heb 3:17: "those who sinned" naming the historical pattern). The continuous present of 1Jo 3:6 is the NT's most precise formal marker of habitual defection.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The defining term is the **Hiphil stem of cha.ta (H2398)**: *heheti* / *wayaḥṭē* — "caused to sin," "made to sin." The H2398 root means to miss the mark, to incur guilt — when placed in the Hiphil causative stem, it means: *to cause another to miss the mark, to make another incur guilt*. The root meaning in its causative form reveals the essential nature of CHAR-7: the leader does not merely sin themselves (the Qal personal action) but makes others sin (the Hiphil causative action). The Hiphil of cha.ta uniquely encodes the transmission mechanism — the leader's action is the cause; the community's sinning is the effect. No Greek vocabulary appears in the 19-verse corpus; the characteristic is entirely Hebrew in its primary vocabulary. The Hiphil causative form is CHAR-7's exclusive grammatical marker — no other sinning characteristic in the corpus uses the Hiphil.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — The primary and exclusive term is **pa.sha (H6586)** in its political-revolt register. The root means *to break away from, to transgress, to revolt* — specifically naming the wilful decisive breaking of a binding relationship. In CHAR-8 the binding relationship is always political-governing (Moab under Israel; Edom under Judah; Israel under the house of David). The root meaning reveals: political revolt is not passive non-compliance but an *active breaking-away* — the pa.sha act has the moral weight of transgression embedded in the root. Pa.sha in the political register confirms that breaking political submission carries the same moral character as transgressing moral-covenantal boundaries — it is wilful, decisive, and morally accountable. No NT Greek vocabulary appears in the 9-verse corpus; the characteristic is entirely OT Hebrew.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The primary and exclusive terms are **blasfēmia (G0988)** — noun — and **blasfēmos (G0989)** — adjective. The root combines *blapto* (to harm, to damage) and *phēmi* (to speak, to say — related to *phōnē*, voice). The compound root meaning: *harmful speech, speech that damages*. The root reveals that sinful speech is defined not by its doctrinal content alone (a claim about God) but by its *effect*: it harms. Both the slander register (VCG-01 — person-directed harmful speech) and the blasphemy register (VCG-02/03 — God-directed presumptuous speech) are subsumed under this single root, revealing that the Greek term covers a unified semantic field: speech that damages, whether the target is God or persons. No OT Hebrew vocabulary appears in the 22-verse corpus — the characteristic is exclusively NT Greek, confirming that CHAR-9 as a distinct named characteristic is a NT conceptual configuration.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — Three distinct Greek terms, each with its own root. (1) **deleazō (G1185)** — from *delear* (bait, lure): the fishing/hunting metaphor embedded in the root — to place bait before a creature to draw it toward capture. Jam 1:14 — "lured and enticed by his own desire" — the root reveals that enticement is a bait-and-capture operation; the person's desire is the point where the bait attaches. (2) **sunupokrinomai (G4942)** — *sun-* (together) + *hupokrinomai* (to play a theatrical role, to act a part): the theatrical metaphor reveals that collective hypocrisy is a joint performance — the community is on stage together, playing a role that does not match their true identity. (3) **apostasia (G0646)** — *apo-* (away from) + *stasis* (standing, position): the standing-away-from root reveals that apostasy is a positional-departure — the person has moved from their prior standing (covenantal position) to a new position of standing-away-from. No OT Hebrew vocabulary appears in the 5-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Four term-groups across the 112-verse corpus. (1) **H2403B chat.tat** (Gen 4:7): noun derived from H2398 cha.ta — "to miss the mark, to incur guilt." As a noun, chat.tat names the sin-entity itself (not the sinning act) — the sin crouching at the door is a noun-power, an entity with desire and purpose. The noun form reveals that CHAR-11 is the sin-as-entity dimension of the H2398 root. (2) **H7564 rish.ah** (Isa 9:18; Mal 1:4; 3:15; 4:1): wickedness as abstract quality — the state of being wicked as a settled inner condition; related to rasha (the wicked person). (3) **G0266 hamartia**: the dominant NT noun — derived from the same root as the verb hamartanō (to sin, to miss the mark). As noun, hamartia names sin-as-condition, sin-as-power (Rom 5:21 — "sin reigned"; Rom 7:17 — "sin that dwells"). The noun's personification throughout Romans 5-8 is CHAR-11's most distinctive lexical feature: sin is addressed as a subject with agency, desires, and a governing function. (4) **G3900 paraptōma**: trespass — from *para* (beside/aside) + *pipto* (to fall) — a falling-aside, a false step. Names the relational-offense dimension: trespass is not merely missing the mark but falling aside from the path, with relational implications (Rom 4:25 — "delivered up for our trespasses").

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — Two term-groups. (1) **hamartia (G0266)** — noun — deployed in the power-governing register: Joh 8:34 — "slave to sin" (*doulos tēs hamartias* — genitive: sin as the master/owner); Gal 3:22 — "imprisoned everything under sin" (*hypo hamartian* — accusative with hypo: sin as the power under which everything is confined). The noun's genitive and accusative deployments here name sin as an active ruling subject with ownership and confining authority — not merely an act or state but a governing agent. (2) **hamartanō (G0264)** — verb — in the present-continuous habitual register: 1Jo 3:8/9 — *hamartanōn* (present active participle — "making a practice of sinning"), *hamartanein* (present infinitive — "to keep on sinning"), *poiein tēn hamartian* (phrase — "to make sin," i.e. to practise it); 1Jo 5:16/18 — *hamartanonta* / *hamartanōn* (present participles naming ongoing sinning). The present-tense continuous forms carry the characteristic's defining grammar: the enslaving power is constituted by and evidenced in *sustained ongoing* sinning, not episodic acts.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Five term-groups across the 205 verses. (1) **H2403B chat.tat** (VCG-05 — 113 verses): the dominant noun — derived from H2398 cha.ta ("miss the mark"). As a noun, chat.tat names the sin-entity, the act-as-fact retained before God. The noun form makes sin a thing that persists: "the sin which he has committed" (Lev 4:23) — the committed sin is now an object that requires remedy. (2) **H2401/H2403A cha.ta.ah** (VCG-02 — 9 verses): a feminine noun form, naming sin as an objective moral category. Jer 17:1 — "the sin of Judah is written" — cha.ta.ah as the subject of the writing metaphor, naming sin as the inscribed entity. (3) **H2399 chet** (VCG-01 — 32 verses): the personal-liability noun — "that man shall bear his sin" (Num 9:13); "each one shall be put to death for his own sin" (Deu 24:16). Chet names sin as a personal burden carried by the individual. (4) **H2398 cha.ta** (verb — multiple VCG-05 verses): "whoever has sinned against me" (Exo 32:33); "your sin will find you out" (Num 32:23) — the verb form names the act that creates the record entry. (5) **G0266 hamartia / G0265 hamartēma** (NT — Joh 1:29; Rom 3:25): the Greek equivalents — hamartia (the sin of the world as a collective burden); hamartēma (individual sinful acts — Rom 3:25 — "former sins" passed over).

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Four term-groups. (1) **kip.pu.rim (H3725)** — plural noun from kāpar: "coverings, atonements." The root kāpar means to cover, to smear, to make expiation. The covering metaphor is the OT's primary forgiveness-image: sin is not destroyed but covered so that divine judgment does not fall upon it. The plural form kip.pu.rim names the institution rather than a single act: the Day of Coverings, the covering-system. (2) **chat.tat (H2403B/H2403H)** — the sin-offering: the animal whose death covers the sin; the term names both the sin committed and the offering that addresses it, revealing their inseparability in the OT economy. (3) **cha.ta.ah (H2401)** — the sin as the moral category requiring covering (Exo 32:30 — "make atonement for your sin"). (4) **hamartia (G0266) / hamartēma (G0265) / paraptōma (G3900)** — NT terms: hamartia as the sin whose forgiveness is declared (Mat 26:28 — "for the forgiveness of sins"); hamartēma (individual sinful act — Mar 3:28/29); paraptōma (trespass — Eph 1:7; Col 2:13; 2Cor 5:19 — the relational offence not counted against).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — The sole primary term across all 8 verses is **cha.ta (H2398)** — the verb "to miss the mark, to sin, to incur guilt." The root meaning (missing the mark) reveals that generational sin is not conceptually separated from ordinary sinning at the lexical level: the inherited condition is transmitted through and as the same sinning acts that cha.ta names in its individual-act register. CHAR-15 has no specialised vocabulary for its distinctive feature (the generational inheritance mechanism); the inherited condition is named through the same verb as individual wilful sinning, applied to ancestors ("your first father sinned" — Isa 43:27) and to successive generations ("they sinned still more" — Psa 78:17). No NT Greek vocabulary appears in the 8-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Two primary terms. (1) **chat.ta (H2400)** — OT agent-noun from the cha.ta root ("miss the mark"). The agent-noun form (*qattāl* pattern in Hebrew) indicates habitual or intensive action: chat.ta names not one who has sinned once but one whose character is constitutively defined by sinning. Gen 13:13 — "great sinners" (*chat.ta.im gĕdōlîm*) — the plural agent-noun names a class of persons constituted by extreme habitual sinning. (2) **hamartōlos (G0268)** — NT noun/adjective from hamartanō ("to sin, to miss the mark"). Hamartōlos functions both as a noun ("the sinner" — Luk 7:37) and as an adjective ("sinful man" — Luk 5:8; "sinful generation" — Mar 8:38). The root reveals: the sinner-identity is defined by the same "missing the mark" as ordinary sinning but at the level of constituted character rather than discrete acts.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Five primary term-groups. (1) **a.sham (H0816)** — verb "to be guilty, to become guilty, to realize one's guilt" — dominant in VCG-01's guilt-recognition sequences (Lev 4:13/22/27; 5:2/3/4/5/17/19; Num 5:6; Hos 5:15). The root (*ʾāšam*) means to offend, to incur guilt — the verb form names the becoming-guilty moment and the realising-of-guilt moment. (2) **a.shem (H0818)** — noun "guilty one" — Gen 42:21; Ezr 10:19. (3) **ash.mah (H0819)** — noun "guilt, guiltiness" — dominant in VCG-02's accumulation passages (Ezr 9:6/7/13/15; 2Ch 24:18/28:10/13/33:23). The noun form names the guilt-condition as an accumulated state. (4) **a.von (H5771H)** — "iniquity, guilt, liability" — VCG-03's transferable-burden register (Gen 44:16; Exo 28:38; 2Sa 14:9; Jer 33:8). (5) **a.von (H5771I)** — "punishment, punitive consequence" — VCG-04's punitive register (Gen 4:13; Eze 4:4/5/6). (6) **pu.qah (H6330)** — "staggering, stumbling" — 1Sa 25:31 — the single-term expression of conscience-stagger under guilt. No NT Greek appears in this corpus.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — Single primary term throughout: **a.von (H5771G)** — the crime/moral-wrong sub-entry. The root (*ʿāwôn*) derives from a verbal root meaning "to be bent, crooked, twisted" — naming sin as moral deviance from the straight path. In its H5771G crime-sense, the noun names the accumulated moral wrongdoing itself — the twisted inner reality — not merely the act or the punishment. The root's "crookedness" metaphor is significant: iniquity is the constitutive moral distortion of the person's inner orientation, not merely an external act. The "crime" register distinguishes H5771G from the guilt-register (H5771H — the moral liability arising from the crime) and the punishment-register (H5771I — the penal consequence). No NT Greek appears in this 162-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Four primary term-families. (1) **pe.sha (H6588)** / **pa.sha (H6586)** — noun/verb "transgression/to transgress, to rebel, to break away" — OT dominant (115 verses); root *pāšaʿ* means "to break away from, to revolt, to rebel" — naming the act as a relational-political breaking-away from authority. The root is the vocabulary of political rebellion applied to the moral-theological sphere; (2) **sa.rah (H5627)** — "revolt, turning aside, apostasy" — 7 verses in VCG-02; root *sārar* — to turn aside, to rebel — names the inner defiance as an orientation-reversal; (3) **parabasis (G3847) / parabatēs (G3848) / parabainō (G3845)** — NT "transgression/transgressor/to transgress" — 15 verses; Greek compound *para* (beside/past) + *bainō* (to go, to step) — literally "stepping past/beside" — the boundary-crossing spatial metaphor made explicit; (4) **paraptōma (G3900)** — "trespass, false step, lapse" — 5 verses (VCG-05 Adam-paradigm); Greek *para* + *piptō* (to fall beside) — a stumbling aside from the right path.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Two primary term-families, exclusively OT Hebrew (no NT vocabulary). (1) **ma.al (H4603/H4604)** — verb and noun "to commit a breach of faith, to act unfaithfully, to trespass against sacred things"; from a root meaning "to cover up, to conceal, to act covertly" — naming faithlessness as a concealed inner breach; the ma.al-faithlessness is the hidden betrayal of what was owed; used primarily for unfaithfulness toward God and sacred things (VCG-01 dominant); 1Ch 10:13 — "breach of faith with the Lord." (2) **ba.gad (H0898)** — verb "to act treacherously, to be faithless, to deal deceitfully"; root meaning relates to garment-covering (clothing that covers while hiding) or to dealing deceitfully; the ba.gad-treachery is the betrayal that wears a friendly face; used more for interpersonal treachery (VCG-02 dominant) and constitutional character (VCG-03). The two roots together reveal: ma.al names the sacred-covenantal breach; ba.gad names the relational-interpersonal betrayal.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Nine term-families spanning OT and NT. (1) **tah.pu.khah (H8419)** — "perverseness, frowardness" from root *hāpak* — "to turn, to overturn"; names what has been overturned from its proper state; (2) **la.zut (H3891)** — "perversity, crookedness" — Pro 4:24; (3) **sa.laph (H5557)** — "to subvert, to overthrow, to pervert" — root sense of overturning foundations; used for judgment-perversion (VCG-02); (4) **a.vah (H5753A/B)** — "to be crooked, to twist, to distort" — the verbal form "to do iniquity" by twisting what was straight; (5) **te.vel (H8397)** — "perversion, confusion" from a root meaning "to mix, to confuse" — names the violation of created-order categories; (6) **sur (H5494)** — "to turn aside, to degenerate" — the vine turning wild (Jer 2:21); (7) **cha.val (H2254B)** — "to destroy, to ruin, to corrupt" — M03 cross-register; (8) **nav.lut (H5040)** — "lewdness, shamelessness" — M07 cross-register (Hos 2:10); (9) **ftheirō (G5351) / fthora (G5356) / diaftheirō (G1311)** — NT "to destroy/corrupt/corruption" — the Greek family for moral and physical decay. Together the terms reveal: perversion as the overturning of the proper order (tah.pu.khah/sa.laph), the mixing of what should be kept separate (te.vel), the twisting of what should be straight (a.vah/sur), and the decay/ruin of what was good (cha.val/ftheirō/fthora).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Five primary term-families. (1) **a.vel (H5766A)** / **av.lah (H5766B)** — noun/verb "injustice, wrong, violence, wickedness" — root *ʿāwal* meaning "to act unjustly, to be crooked in dealings"; names the act and condition of moral-conduct wrongness; (2) **av.val (H5767)** — "the unjust one, the unrighteous person" — agent-noun from *ʿāwal*; (3) **a.vil (H5760)** — "ungodly, morally lawless" — from a root denoting moral worthlessness; (4) **adikos (G0094)** — NT "unjust, unrighteous" — Greek compound *a-* (not) + *dikē* (justice, right); literally "not-right/not-just"; the alpha-privative construction names injustice as the negation of justice; (5) **adikēma (G0092)** — NT "wrongdoing, crime, injustice" — the act-noun; the specific deed of injustice. Together the terms reveal: injustice as crookedness in dealings (*ʿāwal*), as person-type (*av.val/adikos*), and as specific legal-moral crime (*adikēma*) — three levels of the same moral failure.

---

### T7.1.2

**Question:** What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the characteristic operates?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Cha.ta (H2398) operates as: (1) **Qal verb** — the active sinning act ("the soul who sins," Eze 18:4; "I have sinned," 2Sa 12:13; "they sinned against me," Eze 14:13). (2) **Piel verb** (intensive/causative) — "making/causing to sin" (not in this corpus directly but underlying the causative sense in 1Ki 14:16 — Jeroboam who "made Israel to sin," which belongs to CHAR-7). (3) **Hiphil** — causative. In VCG-04 the Lev 4/5 corpus uses the noun form chat.tat alongside the verb. Hamartanō (G0264) is similarly verbal throughout — an action-term not a state-term. The grammatical range reveals that sinning is *event-language* not *condition-language*: the primary grammatical form names a discrete act, not a standing state. This confirms that CHAR-1 is constitutively an act rather than a condition.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Cha.ta in CHAR-2 operates as: (1) **Qal verb with adverbial modifier** (cha.ta + bishgagah: Lev 4:2; Num 15:27/28; Num 22:34) — an action modified by the inner-quality qualifier. (2) **Piel verb (denominative — VCG-02)**: Exo 29:36 ("you shall purify the altar"), Lev 8:15, Eze 43:20/22/45:18 — cha.ta used as a ritual process verb meaning to remove sin/defilement from an object. (3) **Noun form (chat.ta.ah)**: Lev 9:15 ("the goat of the sin offering") — the characteristic transformed into an institutional object (the offering). The grammatical range reveals that the same root covers both the human act of sinning and the remedial process applied to persons and sacred objects — a grammatical unity that reflects the single theological framework of sin-and-remedy.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — In the confession-mode, cha.ta operates almost exclusively as a **first-person perfect verb**: *chatati* (I have sinned) or *chatanu* (we have sinned). This grammatical configuration reveals two things: (1) *Self-application*: the first person makes the speaker the agent of the named sin — "I" not "they" or "he" sinned. (2) *Past-completion*: the perfect aspect names the act as completed — it is already done; confession names a fait accompli, not a future intention or a general principle. The grammatical precision of the confessional form thus encodes the moral precision of genuine confession: it names a specific completed act by a specific identified person. No other grammatical configuration carries this confessional weight.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The grammatical range within the CHAR-4 corpus: (1) *Negated perfect* (Jer 2:35 — *lo chatati*): the completed act of sinning denied; (2) *Participial/nominal* (Ecc 2:26; 8:12 — *hachotet*): the sinning person as constituted type; (3) *Interrogative noun* (Jer 16:10 — the sin unrecognised and questioned); (4) *NT present infinitive/participle* (1Cor 15:34 — ongoing sinning in a state of suppression); (5) *NT adjective/participial* (Tit 3:11 — the person as "sinful" — a settled character description). The grammatical range reveals that conscience suppression can be expressed at every grammatical level: the denial of a completed act, the constituted type, the unrecognised noun, the ongoing present action, and the settled character description.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The grammatical range of the primary construction: (1) *Negated movement verb + preposition + sin-noun* (lo sur min + chat.tat): this is a predicate negation construction — it names what did not happen (turning/departing) relative to a specified object (the sins). (2) *Perfect/imperfect verb* of clinging (davaq — 2Ki 3:3): the perfect aspect of "clung to" names a completed act of attachment with ongoing effect. (3) *Hiphil stem* of the hardening verbs (Neh 9:29 — qasha, sarar): the Hiphil makes these causative — they actively caused their neck to stiffen, their shoulder to be stubborn. (4) *NT present participle* (hamartanontōn — 1Ti 5:20; Heb 10:26): ongoing action, active voice — sinning that continues. The grammatical range reveals: refusal to repent is expressed as both *completed adherence* (perfect davaq) and *continued ongoing action* (present participle hamartanō) — the will's past commitment to non-departure and its present continuation.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The grammatical range covers all major categories: (1) *Noun/participial person-type*: hachotet (Ecc 7:26; 9:2/18; Pro 11:31/13:22) — the most characteristic CHAR-6 form, naming the constituted sinner; (2) *Qal perfect verb with iterative modifier*: "sinned yet again" (Exo 9:34) — completed acts accumulated through repetition; (3) *Qal perfect with continuative*: "you have sinned... there they have continued" (Hos 10:9) — completed act + continuation; (4) *NT present continuous participle*: hamartanōn (1Jo 3:6) — the ongoing continuous state as the characteristic's definitive NT form; (5) *NT constative aorist*: hēmarton (Heb 3:17) — viewing the extended historical sinning pattern as a single unit. The grammatical range reveals that habitual defection is expressed through the *person-type*, *iterative/continuous*, and *pattern-viewing* grammatical configurations — all of which distinguish settled pattern from single act.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The Hiphil of cha.ta appears across the corpus in three forms: (1) *Hiphil perfect*: *heheti* — "he made to sin" (completed action — 1Ki 14:16); (2) *Hiphil imperfect/wayyiqtol*: *wayaḥṭē* — narrative past: "and he made to sin" (the ongoing narrative sequence — repeated across Kings); (3) *Hiphil infinitive construct*: *lehaḥṭi* — "to cause to sin" (Jer 32:35 — "to cause Judah to sin"). These grammatical forms cover the completed past (the historical act), the narrative past (the sequence of kings), and the purposive infinitive (the intentional causative — built the high places for the purpose of causing Judah to sin). The range reveals that contagious sin is expressed as: completed historical acts, recurring narrative patterns, and deliberate purposive construction.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Pa.sha appears in three forms across the corpus: (1) *Qal perfect*: "has been in rebellion" (1Ki 12:19; 2Ch 10:19 — the state of ongoing revolt as a completed and persisting condition); (2) *Qal wayyiqtol (narrative past)*: "rebelled" (2Ki 1:1; 3:5 — the sequential narrative past: Moab rebelled at a specific historical moment); (3) *Qal perfect / compound verb*: "revolted from the rule of... and set up a king of their own" (2Ki 8:20; 2Ch 21:8 — the act plus its positive constructive consequence). The grammatical range covers: completed ongoing state (perfect), narrative past event (wayyiqtol), and compound act with consequence. This range reveals that political revolt can be: an established ongoing condition (Israel's rebellion — "to this day"), a specific historical event (Moab's rebellion — "after the death of Ahab"), or an act with positive constructive consequence (Edom setting up its own king).

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The grammatical range covers: (1) *Noun (blasfēmia)*: "the blasphemy against the Spirit will not be forgiven" (Mat 12:31 — the act named as a noun); "slander" (Eph 4:31; Col 3:8 — the act in community context); "blasphemous names" (Rev 13:1 — the noun used attributively); (2) *Adjective (blasfēmos)*: "blasphemous words" (Act 6:11 — qualifying the words); "a blasphemous judgment" (Jude 9; 2Pe 2:11 — qualifying the speech-act); "abusive" (2Ti 3:2 — the dispositional adjective naming the person); (3) *Verb (blasfēmeō — implied in the nominal form)*: "He is blaspheming!" (Mar 2:7 — verb form); "to utter blasphemies against God" (Rev 13:6 — verbal phrase). The range covers act (noun), quality (adjective), and ongoing action (verb), showing the characteristic operates as event, property, and continuous practice.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The grammatical range covers distinct forms per term. (1) *deleazō*: (a) verb aorist passive "lured" + verb aorist passive "enticed" (Jam 1:14 — two passive forms, naming the person being drawn); (b) verb present active "they entice" (2Pe 2:14 — active, naming the enticers' ongoing action); (c) verb present active "they entice" (2Pe 2:18 — active). The active/passive distinction reveals two different perspectives: the enticed person (passive) and the enticing practitioner (active). (2) *sunupokrinomai*: verb aorist indicative "acted hypocritically along with him" (Gal 2:13 — single past event). (3) *apostasia*: noun (Act 21:21 — naming the condition/teaching as a category). The grammatical range is narrow given the 5-verse corpus.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The grammatical range of hamartia is the most distinctive and analytically significant. (1) *Noun with personal agency (personification)*: Rom 5:21 — "sin reigned"; Rom 7:8 — "sin, seizing an opportunity"; Rom 7:11 — "sin deceived me"; Rom 7:17 — "sin that dwells within me" — the noun is used as the subject of active verbs (reign, seize, deceive, dwell), personifying the condition as an agent with will and strategy. (2) *Noun with prepositional phrase* ("under sin" — Rom 3:9; "in your sins" — Joh 8:21/24; "dead in sins" — Eph 2:1) — naming a condition of location/position relative to the condition's power. (3) *Noun in genitive/qualification* ("body of sin" — Rom 6:6; "law of sin" — Rom 7:23/25; "sinful flesh" — Rom 8:3) — qualifying other nouns with the sin-condition. The verb form hamartanō appears in universalisation statements: Rom 3:23 — "all have sinned" (past tense — completed-state universalisation). The grammatical range reveals: CHAR-11's condition is expressed primarily through *nominal* and *positional* grammar — sin as a noun-entity, a location, a law — rather than through action-verbs.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The grammatical range is the most analytically significant feature of CHAR-12's vocabulary. (1) *Noun in genitive ownership*: Joh 8:34 — *doulos tēs hamartias* — sin in the genitive names it as the owner/master; the genitive of ownership is the enslaving-power's most precise grammatical expression. (2) *Noun under preposition*: Gal 3:22 — *hypo hamartian* — sin as the confining power under which everything is placed; the hypo + accusative construction names sin as an overarching covering authority. (3) *Verb in present participle*: 1Jo 3:8/9; 5:16/18 — the present participle (*hamartanōn* — the one who is sinning, present and ongoing) names the continuous state of sinning that characterises the enslaved person. (4) *Negative present infinitive*: 1Jo 3:9 — "cannot keep on sinning" (*ou dynatai hamartanein*) — the grammatical impossibility of ongoing sinning is the liberation-statement; the present infinitive names what is now constitutionally foreclosed by the new birth. The range reveals: CHAR-12 is grammatically constituted by noun-mastery constructions and present-continuous verb forms — the enslaving power is ongoing and the captivity is a sustained state.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The grammatical range of chat.tat (H2403B) is the most analytically significant. (1) *Noun as subject of divine action*: Exo 32:32 — "if you will forgive their sin" — sin as the direct object of the forgiveness request; Isa 43:25 — "I will not remember your sins" — sin as the object of divine non-remembrance; (2) *Noun in possessive construction*: "my sin" (Psa 38:3), "their sins" (Lev 26:18), "his sin" (Lev 4:26) — the possessive marks the personal ownership of the record; (3) *Noun as the subject of a finding*: Exo 32:34 — "I will visit their sin upon them" — sin as the direct object of divine visitation; Hos 13:12 — "his sin is kept in store" — sin as the object of divine storage. The grammatical range moves between object (of divine action) and possession (of the human person) — naming both the divine handling and the personal ownership of the record.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Kip.pu.rim (H3725) appears exclusively as a noun in the corpus — "Day of Atonement" (Lev 23:27/28; 25:9), "sin offering of atonement" (Num 29:11), "ram of atonement" (Num 5:8; Exo 30:16). The noun form names the atoning-institution rather than the atoning-act (kāpar as verb would name the act). Chat.tat appears as noun — sin/sin-offering (Lev 4:3/14/5:6/10/10:17/19; 2Ch 29:23/24) — consistently naming the offering-vehicle. In the NT: hamartia appears in the genitive of purpose — "for the forgiveness of sins" (*eis aphesin tōn hamartiōn* — Mat 26:28; Act 2:38) — naming sin as the object of forgiveness rather than as agent. The grammatical range: OT terms primarily nominal (institution-naming); NT terms primarily in purpose-constructions (naming what forgiveness addresses).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Cha.ta appears in the following grammatical forms across the 8 verses. (1) *Qal perfect* — "sinned" (past completed act): Isa 43:27 — *chāṭaʾ* ("your first father sinned"); Isa 64:5 — *chāṭāʾnû* ("we sinned"); Jer 8:14 — *chāṭāʾnû* ("we have sinned"); (2) *Qal imperfect with waw* — "sinned still more" / "they still sinned": Psa 78:17 — *wayyôsîpû lachəṭô* (literally "they added to sin" — indicating continuation); Psa 78:32 — *wayêchəṭûʾ* ("they sinned"); (3) *Qal perfect plural* — Isa 64:5 — *chāṭāʾnû* — first-person plural confession; Jer 8:14 — same. The grammatical range reveals: past tense (ancestral sinning completed — Isa 43:27), continuation tense (ongoing sinning — Psa 78:17/32), and corporate perfect (community's completed sin-state — Isa 64:5; Jer 8:14). The "sinned still more" form (*wayyôsîpû lachəṭô*) is particularly distinctive: it names escalating continuation, not merely repetition.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Wide for hamartōlos (G0268). (1) *Noun — definite person-type*: "the sinner" (Luk 7:37; Luk 18:13 — "a sinner"; 1Ti 1:15 — "sinners" as salvific target); (2) *Noun — indefinite classification*: Mat 9:10 — "tax collectors and sinners" — the pairing identifies a social class; (3) *Noun — self-designation*: Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man"; 1Ti 1:15 — "of whom I am the foremost"; (4) *Adjective — characterising a generation*: Mar 8:38 — "this sinful generation"; Luk 24:7 — "sinful men." For chat.ta (H2400): (1) *Noun plural — identifying a class*: Gen 13:13 — "great sinners"; (2) *Noun — identifying a people*: 1Sa 15:18 — "the sinners, the Amalekites"; (3) *Collective adjective*: Amo 9:8 — "the sinful kingdom." The grammatical range spans from individual self-designation (Luk 18:13) to collective characterisation of peoples (1Sa 15:18) and generations (Mar 8:38).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — A.sham (H0816) spans the broadest grammatical range: (1) *Qal perfect* — "they realized their guilt" (Lev 4:13 — *wĕnĕʾšāmû*); (2) *Qal imperfect* — "he shall be guilty" / "he is guilty" (Lev 5:17/19); (3) *Qal participle* — "those who are guilty" (Judg 21:22 — *ʾāšēm*); (4) *Niphal* — "became guilty" (Gen 42:21 — *ʾăbāl ʾăšēmîm*). Ash.mah (H0819) functions as a noun throughout — "the guilt" (Ezr 9:6/7/13/15). A.von (H5771H) functions as a noun — "the guilt/iniquity" (Exo 28:38 — "bear the guilt"). Pu.qah (H6330) is a noun — "cause of stumbling/pangs" (1Sa 25:31). The grammatical range from verb (becoming-guilty moment) through noun (guilt-condition-state) maps the characteristic's arc from event to sustained state.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — A.von (H5771G) functions exclusively as a noun throughout the corpus, spanning singular and plural forms. (1) *Singular — personal*: Psa 32:5 — "I did not cover my iniquity" (*ʿăwōnî* — "my iniquity"); Eze 18:20 — "the wickedness of the wicked shall be upon himself" (*ʿăwōn* — singular noun); (2) *Plural — accumulated*: Psa 38:4 — "my iniquities have gone over my head" (*ʿăwōnōtāy* — "my iniquities" plural); Isa 53:6 — "the Lord has laid on him the iniquity of us all" (singular collective); Ezr 9:6 — "our iniquities have risen higher than our heads" (plural); (3) *Construct state — relational*: Gen 15:16 — "the iniquity of the Amorites" (*ʿăwōn hāʾĕmōrî* — genitive construct naming whose iniquity); Exo 20:5 — "iniquity of the fathers" (genitive). The grammatical range from singular personal to plural accumulated to collective universal (Isa 53:6) covers the full scope of the characteristic.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Wide across both OT and NT. (1) *Pe.sha (H6588)*: used as noun throughout — singular (Psa 32:1 — "whose transgression is forgiven") and plural (Psa 51:1 — "blot out my transgressions"; Amos 1:3 — "for three transgressions of Damascus"); (2) *Pa.sha (H6586)*: verb form — Qal active (Eze 2:3 — "who have rebelled against me"; Jer 2:29 — "you have all transgressed against me"); Hiphil causative (Amos 4:4 — "come to Bethel and transgress"); (3) *Parabasis (G3847)*: noun — "the transgression" (Rom 4:15; Gal 3:19; Heb 2:2/9:15); *parabatēs (G3848)*: agent-noun "transgressor" (Rom 2:25/27; Gal 2:18; Jam 2:9/11); *parabainō (G3845)*: verb "to transgress/break" (Mat 15:2/3; Act 1:25; 2Jo 9); (4) *Paraptōma (G3900)*: noun — "trespass" (Rom 5:15/16/17/18/20). The grammatical range — from noun to verb to agent-noun — covers the act (verb), the event (noun), and the person constituted by the act (agent-noun).

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Wide across both terms. (1) *Ma.al (H4603)*: verb form — "acted faithlessly" (*māʿal*) — Eze 14:13; 2Ch 26:16/36:14; noun form H4604 (*māʿal*) — "breach of faith" — 1Ch 10:13 — "died for his breach of faith"; "faithlessness" — Ezr 9:2/4; 2Ch 33:19. Both verb and noun cover the same semantic range; (2) *Ba.gad (H0898)*: Qal active — "dealt treacherously" (*bāgad*) — Jer 3:20; Mal 2:14; Hos 6:7; agent-noun — "the treacherous" (*bōgĕdîm*) — Psa 119:158 — "I look at the faithless"; Isa 24:16 — "the traitors have betrayed"; "treacherous" (*bāgĕdāh*) — Jer 3:8; Psa 25:3 — "those who are wantonly treacherous." The grammatical range — verb (act), noun (event/condition), and agent-noun (person) — covers the act, the condition, and the person constituted by the act.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Wide across all term-families. (1) *A.vah (H5753A/B)*: Qal active verb — "acted wickedly/perversely" (1Ki 8:47; Dan 9:5); participle — "one who commits iniquity" (Psa 106:6); noun form — "twisted mind" (Pro 12:8); (2) *Tah.pu.khah (H8419)*: noun — "perverseness" (Pro 2:12/14; Pro 6:14/8:13/16:28/23:33); (3) *Sa.laph (H5557)*: verb — "subverts/perverts" (Exo 23:8; Pro 21:12/22:12); (4) *Ftheirō (G5351)*: active verb — "corrupts" (1Cor 15:33; 2Cor 7:2; Rev 19:2); passive — "is being corrupted" (Eph 4:22 — *phtheiromenos*); (5) *Fthora (G5356)*: noun — "corruption/decay" (Rom 8:21; Gal 6:8; 2Pe 1:4/2:12/19; 1Cor 15:42/50). The grammatical range covers the act (verb — "perverts"), the condition (passive — "is being corrupted"), the noun-state (tah.pu.khah — "perverseness"), and the noun-consequence (fthora — "corruption/decay").

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Wide across OT and NT. (1) *A.vel (H5766A)*: noun — "injustice/wrong" (Lev 19:15 — "do no injustice in court"; Job 34:10 — "far be it from God that he should do wrong"); (2) *Av.lah (H5766B)*: noun — "wickedness/injustice" (Psa 58:2 — "devise wrongs"; 2Ch 19:7 — "no injustice with the Lord"); (3) *Av.val (H5767)*: agent-noun — "the unrighteous" (Job 27:7 — "be as the unrighteous"; Job 29:17 — "broke the fangs of the unrighteous"); (4) *Adikos (G0094)*: adjective/noun — "unjust/unrighteous" (Mat 5:45 — "on the just and on the unjust"; Luk 16:10 — "dishonest in a very little"; 1Cor 6:9 — "the unrighteous will not inherit"); (5) *Adikēma (G0092)*: act-noun — "wrongdoing/crime" (Act 18:14 — "a matter of wrongdoing"; Rev 18:5 — "her iniquities"). The grammatical range covers the condition (a.vel — wrong-state), the act (adikēma — wrong-deed), and the person (av.val/adikos — wrong-person).

---

### T7.1.3

**Question:** What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — Cha.ta (H2398) operates across: (1) *Directed violation against God* (VCG-01 — the entire God-directed corpus); (2) *Interpersonal wrong* (VCG-02 — "sin against his neighbour," "sin against innocent blood"); (3) *Cultic-legal wrong requiring ritual remedy* (VCG-04 — sin offering system); (4) *Self-directed wrong* (1Cor 6:18 — hamartanō against one's own body; Pro 8:36 — cha.ta against wisdom/self); (5) *Speech-mode wrong* (Psa 39:1, Job 2:10 — sin with tongue/lips); (6) *Missing the way through haste* (Pro 19:2 — broadest semantic reach). The semantic range is wide: from the gravest covenantal violation (Eze 14:13 — land sinning against God) to the most mundane practical missing (Pro 19:2 — haste missing the way). The breadth reveals that cha.ta covers the full spectrum of the will's directional failures.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — Within CHAR-2 specifically, the semantic range of cha.ta + bishgagah covers: (1) *Violation of a divine commandment without deliberate intent* (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27 — the core definition); (2) *Violation arising from ignorance of the morally relevant fact* (Num 22:34 — not knowing the angel stood against him); (3) *Ritual violation arising from situational urgency* (1Sa 14:33/34 — eating with blood in battle); (4) *Cultic defilement of sacred spaces* (VCG-02 — cha.ta as impurity requiring ritual removal). The semantic range is narrower than CHAR-1 by virtue of the *bishgagah* qualifier, which restricts the applicable acts to those lacking deliberate intent. Within that restriction, the range covers individual and communal violations, personal and cultic contexts.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — Within CHAR-3's specific confessional use, the semantic range of *chatati/chatanu* covers: (1) *Vertical offense against God*: "I have sinned against the Lord" (1Sa 7:6; Dan 9:11; Luk 15:21); (2) *Horizontal offense against persons*: "I have sinned against you" (Exo 10:16 — Moses; 2Sa 19:20 — King David); (3) *Self-harm as sinning*: Job 33:27 — "I sinned and perverted what was right"; (4) *Specific act named*: Mat 27:4 — "I have sinned by betraying innocent blood" — the most specific confession in the corpus; (5) *Collective/generational*: "we have sinned" spanning generations (Psa 106:6; Jer 3:25; Lam 5:7). The semantic range within the confessional mode maps the full directional scope of what sinning can be directed against: God, persons, the moral order, and across time.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — Within CHAR-4's specific mode, the semantic range covers: (1) *Denial of committed sin* (Jer 2:35 — "I have not sinned" — active false innocence); (2) *Absence of fear of God* (Ecc 8:12 — the sinner as not-God-fearing — orientation); (3) *Non-pleasing-God existence* (Ecc 2:26 — the sinner defined by not pleasing God); (4) *Ongoing sin enabled by knowledge-absence* (1Cor 15:34 — sin continuing because of spiritual ignorance); (5) *Constituted sinful character* (Tit 3:11 — "sinful" as a settled descriptor). The semantic range is narrower than in CHAR-1/2/3 because CHAR-4's defining feature is the absence of self-recognition rather than the variety of sinning acts.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The sur/lo sur construction's semantic range covers: (1) *physical turning aside* (a person turning from a path); (2) *moral turning from a practice* (departing from a sinful course — the characteristic's primary sense); (3) *complete severance* (removing oneself entirely from a course). In the CHAR-5 corpus, the negated form covers: refusing to turn from inherited sinful worship (Jeroboam's golden calves), refusing to depart from a wrong moral direction, refusing the severance that repentance requires. The davaq root carries the semantic range of attachment: (1) biological cleaving (a man cleaves to his wife); (2) volitional attachment (clinging to a practice or person). Applied to sin, davaq's semantic range reveals the characteristic's attachment dimension: the will cleaves to the sinful course as if in a bond.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — Within CHAR-6's specific deployment, the semantic range covers: (1) *Universal human moral susceptibility*: 1Ki 8:46; Ecc 7:20 — "no one who does not sin" — the baseline of universal sinning; (2) *Sinner as moral identity type*: Ecc 7:26; 9:2; Pro 11:31/13:22 — the person constituted by the sinning orientation; (3) *Sinning as self-reinforcing institutional pattern*: Hos 8:11 — altars for sinning producing more sinning; (4) *Historical-generational persistence*: Hos 10:9 — from Gibeah continued; Heb 3:17 — forty years; (5) *Fundamental indicator of God-relationship absence*: 1Jo 3:6 — "keeps on sinning" as the marker of never having seen or known Christ. The semantic range thus covers the full spectrum from baseline (everyone sins) through constituted sinner-type to eschatological-relational indicator.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — Within the Hiphil mode, the semantic range of the causative covers: (1) *Causing through authority exercise*: 1Ki 16:2 — "made my people Israel to sin" — leadership authority as the causative mechanism; (2) *Causing through structural construction*: Jer 32:35 — "to cause Judah to sin" through building high places — the physical act of building as the causative mechanism; (3) *Causing through cultural teaching*: Deu 20:18 — "not teach you to do according to all their abominable practices" — the teaching-instruction mode as the causative mechanism. The semantic range thus covers three causal pathways: authority, structure, and teaching.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Within CHAR-8's political register, pa.sha covers: (1) *Breaking from governing submission*: "Moab rebelled against Israel" (2Ki 1:1); (2) *Establishing independent governance*: 2Ki 8:20 — "revolted... and set up a king of their own" — the revolt includes the positive assertion of independence; (3) *Ongoing rebellion as a permanent political condition*: 1Ki 12:19 — "Israel has been in rebellion against the house of David to this day" — the present-state of prolonged revolt; (4) *Revolt as politically-militarily significant act requiring response*: 2Ki 3:7 — Moab's revolt is the occasion for military alliance. The semantic range within the political register thus covers: act, ongoing condition, consequence, and political-military significance.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The semantic range across the 22 verses covers: (1) *Person-directed slander*: VCG-01 — harmful speech against persons (Eph 4:31; Col 3:8; Mar 7:22; Mat 15:19); (2) *Divine-authority usurpation*: VCG-02 — speech claiming or appearing to claim divine prerogatives (Mar 2:7; Joh 10:33; Mat 26:65); (3) *Constitutive anti-God defiance*: VCG-03 — blasphemy as the creature's defining orientation (Rev 13:1/5/6; Rev 17:3); (4) *False identity claim*: Rev 2:9 — blasphemy as the false self-presentation that defames what is genuinely God's; (5) *The unforgivable form*: Mat 12:31 — a specific subset of the divine-authority register that carries permanent consequence. The semantic range spans slander through constitutive identity-level defiance.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — (1) *deleazō*: within the corpus — both the enticed victim's experience (Jam 1:14 — passive luring through own desire) and the active enticement of others (2Pe 2:14/18 — enticers deploying the mechanism toward targets). The semantic range thus covers both reception and extension of the mechanism. (2) *sunupokrinomai*: the semantic range within the corpus is narrow (single verse) — joint performance of a false identity alongside others; the sun- prefix restricts it to collective, not individual, hypocrisy. (3) *apostasia*: the semantic range within the corpus covers the accusatory use — the term appears as the charge directed against Paul's teaching (Act 21:21), naming a perceived condition of covenantal departure.

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — The semantic range of hamartia within CHAR-11 covers its widest deployment in the NT: (1) *Universal condition*: Rom 3:9/23 — "under sin... all have sinned"; (2) *Enslaving power*: Rom 5:21 — "sin reigned"; Rom 7:14 — "sold under sin"; (3) *Indwelling force*: Rom 7:17/20 — "sin that dwells within me"; (4) *Law*: Rom 7:23/25 — "law of sin"; (5) *Moral debt*: Mat 9:2 — "your sins are forgiven"; (6) *Death-consequence*: Rom 6:23 — "wages of sin is death"; (7) *Standing guilt*: Joh 9:41 — "your guilt remains." This semantic range is the widest deployment of hamartia in the entire NT corpus — CHAR-11 contains hamartia in every significant mode: power, debt, indwelling, law, consequence, and guilt.

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The semantic range of hamartia/hamartanō within CHAR-12's 9 verses is specifically the *power-governing and practice-constituting range*: (1) *sin as owner-master* (Joh 8:34 — genitive of ownership); (2) *sin as universal imprisoning power* (Gal 3:22 — *hypo hamartian*); (3) *sinning as ongoing practice that constitutes enslavement* (1Jo 3:8 — *hamartanōn*); (4) *sin leading to death* (1Jo 5:16 — the eschatological severity end of the range); (5) *the negated sinning-practice* (1Jo 3:9; 5:18 — what the born-of-God cannot keep doing). The semantic range is narrower than CHAR-11's (which covers all registers of hamartia): CHAR-12 specifically covers the power-ownership and practice-continuity ends of the semantic range.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — The semantic range of chat.tat within CHAR-13's corpus is the widest in M10: (1) *Sin as outcry before God*: Gen 18:20 — "their sin is very grave" — the weight registered before God; (2) *Sin as book-entry*: Exo 32:32/33 — the divine book; (3) *Sin as stored account*: Hos 13:12 — "kept in store"; (4) *Sin as heart-inscription*: Jer 17:1 — "engraved on the tablet of their heart"; (5) *Sin as self-discovering reality*: Num 32:23 — "your sin will find you out"; (6) *Sin as testimony*: Isa 59:12 — "our sins testify against us"; (7) *Sin as burden borne double*: Isa 40:2 — "received from the Lord's hand double for all her sins." This range covers every aspect of the characteristic's definition: recorded, accumulated, named, not hidden, the person carries it.

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Kip.pu.rim within CHAR-14 covers: (1) the altar-consecration atonement (Exo 29:36 — purifying the altar); (2) the annual covering of the people (Lev 23:27/28; 25:9 — Day of Atonement); (3) the ransom-payment atonement (Exo 30:16 — atonement money for lives); (4) the guilt-offering atonement (Num 5:8 — ram of atonement). This range — from altar-purification through personal life-ransom through communal annual covering — reveals kāpar/kip.pu.rim as the most semantically versatile forgiveness-term in the OT. Hamartia in the NT covers: the sin whose forgiveness is announced (Mat 26:28), the sin that leads to eternal non-forgiveness (Mar 3:29), and the sin whose forgiveness opens Spirit-reception (Act 2:38).

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-15]** E — Cha.ta within CHAR-15 covers: (1) *Founding ancestral sinning act* (Isa 43:27 — "your first father sinned"); (2) *Escalating generational continuation* (Psa 78:17 — "sinned still more"); (3) *Persistent corporate sinning despite evidence* (Psa 78:32 — "they still sinned despite his wonders"); (4) *Prolonged community-condition* (Isa 64:5 — "in our sins we have been a long time"); (5) *Corporate-caused doom* (Jer 8:14 — "because we have sinned"); (6) *Past backsliding under divine rescue* (Eze 37:23 — "backslidings in which they have sinned"). The semantic range is narrow (all uses of a single verb) but the contextual variety reveals the characteristic's dimensions: founding act, escalating continuation, prolonged condition, corporate causation, and past-rescue.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Hamartōlos within CHAR-16 covers: (1) *Social category with stigma* (VCG-01): "tax collectors and sinners" (Mat 9:10/11); the woman who "was a sinner" (Luk 7:37); (2) *Self-recognised identity* (VCG-01/02): "I am a sinful man" (Luk 5:8); "be merciful to me, a sinner" (Luk 18:13); (3) *Constituted federal status* (VCG-02): "made sinners" (Rom 5:19); "while we were still sinners" (Rom 5:8); (4) *Target of salvific mission*: "Christ Jesus came to save sinners" (1Ti 1:15); (5) *Moral extreme* (VCG-03): "sinners directed hostility" (Heb 12:3); "ungodly sinners" (Jude 15). Chat.ta covers: (1) extreme habitual type (Gen 13:13 — Sodom); (2) divinely designated enemies (1Sa 15:18 — Amalekites); (3) collective moral characterisation of a people/kingdom (Amo 9:8).

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — The *ʾāšam* family covers: (1) *The recognition moment*: Lev 5:5 — "when he realizes his guilt" — a.sham as the conscience-engagement event; (2) *The incurred state*: Lev 5:19 — "he has indeed incurred guilt before the Lord" — the objective guilt-status; (3) *The accumulated condition*: Ezr 9:6 — "our guilt has mounted up" — ash.mah as the communal guilt-weight; (4) *The condition requiring remedy*: Ezr 10:19 — "their guilt offering was a ram" — the guilt-condition addressed through ritual. A.von (H5771H) covers: *transferable moral burden* (Gen 44:16; Exo 28:38; 2Sa 14:9). A.von (H5771I) covers: *punitive consequence* (Gen 4:13 — "my punishment"; Eze 4:4/5/6 — symbolic bearing). Pu.qah covers: *conscience-stumbling* (1Sa 25:31 — the affective-somatic guilt-experience).

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — A.von (H5771G) within CHAR-18 covers: (1) *Measurable accumulation with threshold*: Gen 15:16 — "not yet complete" — quantifiable moral-crime buildup; (2) *Heart-seated crime*: Eze 14:3 — "stumbling block of their iniquity" rooted in idol-taking into the heart; (3) *Generationally transmitted crime*: Exo 20:5 — "iniquity of the fathers on the children"; (4) *Individually owned crime*: Eze 18:20 — "upon himself" — personal moral-legal attachment; (5) *Overwhelming weight*: Psa 38:4 — "gone over my head; like a heavy burden"; (6) *Self-destructive force*: Pro 5:22 — ensnaring cords; Isa 64:6 — wind carrying away; (7) *Vicariously borne*: Isa 53:6 — laid on the servant. The single term covers seven semantically distinct dimensions within the crime-register.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Pe.sha/pa.sha within CHAR-19 covers: (1) *Interpersonal breach*: Gen 31:36 — "what is my transgression?"; Gen 50:17 — forgiveness for brothers' transgression against Joseph; (2) *Covenant rebellion against God*: Isa 1:2 — "they have rebelled against me"; Hos 8:1 — "transgressed my covenant and rebelled against my law"; (3) *Personal moral breach*: Psa 51:3 — "I know my transgressions"; Job 13:23 — "make me know my transgression"; (4) *Threshold-crossing accumulation*: Amos 1:3/6/9 — "for three transgressions... and for four"; (5) *Oppressive weight*: Lam 1:14 — "transgressions were bound into a yoke." Parabasis covers: (1) *Law-violation*: Rom 4:15; Heb 2:2; (2) *Tradition-breaking*: Mat 15:2/3. Paraptōma covers: (1) *Paradigmatic first trespass*: Rom 5:15/16/17/18; (2) *Law-increasing function*: Rom 5:20.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Ma.al within CHAR-20 covers: (1) *Cultic/sacred trespass*: Lev 5:15 — "breach of faith... in any of the holy things"; Lev 6:2 — "breach of faith against the Lord by deceiving his neighbor"; (2) *Personal covenant-breaking with God*: 1Ch 10:13 — "breach of faith with the Lord in that he did not keep the command"; (3) *Corporate covenant-betrayal*: 1Ch 9:1 — "breach of faith" causing national exile; 2Ch 36:14 — "exceedingly unfaithful" as national disposition. Ba.gad within CHAR-20 covers: (1) *Marital faithlessness*: Num 5:12 — "breaks faith with him"; Mal 2:14 — "been faithless to the wife of your youth"; (2) *Corporate covenant-betrayal toward God*: Jer 3:20 — "treacherous to me, O house of Israel"; Hos 6:7 — "dealt faithlessly with me"; (3) *Constitutional inner character*: Isa 48:8 — "deal treacherously" as foreknown bent; Isa 24:16 — "the traitors have betrayed."

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — The terms collectively cover: (1) *Judgment-subversion*: sa.laph (Exo 23:8 — bribery subverting righteous cause); (2) *Speech-perversion*: tah.pu.khah (Pro 2:12 — perverted speech; Pro 10:31 — perverse tongue); (3) *Heart-perversion and evil-devising*: tah.pu.khah (Pro 6:14 — perverted heart devising evil); (4) *Personal moral twisting*: a.vah (1Ki 8:47; Dan 9:5 — "acted perversely"); (5) *Bodily-prostration from sin*: a.vah (Psa 38:6 — "utterly bowed down"); (6) *Created-order violation*: te.vel (Lev 18:23 — bestiality; Lev 20:12 — incest); (7) *Degenerative transformation*: sur (Jer 2:21 — turned degenerate wild vine); (8) *Desire-driven progressive corruption*: ftheirō/fthora (Eph 4:22; 2Pe 1:4); (9) *Cosmic bondage to decay*: fthora (Rom 8:21 — creation's bondage to corruption).

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — The terms collectively cover: (1) *Judicial injustice*: a.vel (Lev 19:15 — "no injustice in court"; Psa 82:2 — "judge unjustly"); (2) *Commercial injustice*: a.vel (Lev 19:35 — "no wrong in measures"); (3) *Violent oppression*: av.lah (2Sa 7:10 — "violent men"; Psa 58:2 — "deal out violence"); (4) *Speech-injustice*: av.lah (Job 6:30 — "is there any injustice on my tongue?"; Isa 59:3 — "tongue mutters wickedness"); (5) *Character-level injustice*: adikos (Luk 16:10 — "dishonest in very little and in much"); (6) *Legal-actionable wrongdoing*: adikēma (Act 18:14 — "a matter of wrongdoing or vicious crime"); (7) *Cosmic-scale crime*: adikēma (Rev 18:5 — "God has remembered her iniquities").

---

### T7.1.4

**Question:** Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The vocabulary cluster across M10 achieves some of these distinctions. The act/condition distinction is partly served by cha.ta (act) versus chat.tat (H2403B — the named sin as an ongoing record, CHAR-13's territory) versus chat.ta (H2400 — the sinner as a constituted character, CHAR-16's territory). Within CHAR-1's own corpus, paraptōma (G3900, Gal 6:1) introduces a nuance — "caught in a transgression" suggests a condition of being-caught rather than simply the act. Hamartanō throughout VCG-05 treats sinning as an action-event. The vocabulary does distinguish act from constituted character (cha.ta vs chat.ta) but does not have a dedicated term for the received/given distinction within the CHAR-1 corpus.

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The vocabulary in this corpus distinguishes act from condition through the sequence of terms. The act itself (cha.ta + bishgagah — inadvertent sinning) is described at the moment of occurrence (Lev 4:2; Num 15:27). The resulting condition (guilt) is named in Lev 5:5 ("realizes his guilt" — H0819 ash.mah or contextual guilt-term in the broader Lev 5 passage) and in Lev 5:1 ("he shall bear his iniquity" — H5771 a.von). The remedy object (chat.ta.ah H2403 — sin offering) names the institutional response to the condition. The sequence act → condition → remedy is lexically marked by distinct terms, confirming that the vocabulary distinguishes the sinning event from its moral residue and from its institutional address.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The vocabulary within CHAR-3's corpus partially distinguishes act from condition. The confessional act itself (*chatati*) names the sin as an act committed. The guilt-condition that precedes and grounds confession is evidenced by *yadat* (to know — 2Sa 19:20) and the heart-struck idiom (2Sa 24:10) — these name the inner condition. The resulting forgiven-condition is named by *lo yizzaker* (not be remembered — Eze 33:16). The vocabulary does not have a dedicated confession-term (no word that specifically means "to confess" appears in this corpus's primary sinning-vocabulary) — it uses the sinning-vocabulary self-referentially. The confession-receipt vocabulary (*la.mad* — to hear, *shama* — to listen, Neh 1:6) appears on the divine-reception side.

**[CHAR-4] Conscience suppression** *(E)*

**[CHAR-4]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes two aspects: (1) *Act-denial* (Jer 2:35 — the denial of a specific completed sinning act) vs (2) *Character/condition* (Ecc 2:26; 8:12; Tit 3:11 — the sinner as a constituted type or condition rather than a single act). This act-vs-condition distinction maps onto the characteristic's two primary modes: active denial of a specific sin (act-focused) and habituated conscience-absent sinning (condition-focused). No dedicated vocabulary for the denial/suppression mechanism itself exists — the characteristic borrows the sinning vocabulary in its inverted or sinner-type forms.

**[CHAR-5] Refusal to repent** *(E)*

**[CHAR-5]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes two aspects: (1) *Passive non-departure* (lo sur min — did not depart from): the absence of the turning act, expressed as a negated movement; (2) *Active attachment* (davaq — clung to): the presence of an adhering bond to the sinful course. These two aspects (absence of the turn vs presence of the bond) are not the same: passive non-departure does not require active clinging; active clinging implies a more advanced stage of the characteristic. The Neh 9:29 hardening vocabulary (qasha — stiffened; sarar — stubborn) adds a third aspect: *active resistance to correction*, which is distinct from both passive non-departure and active clinging.

**[CHAR-6] Habitual defection** *(E)*

**[CHAR-6]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes *act* from *person-type* through grammatical form: the verb (cha.ta — sinning act) vs the participial-noun (hachotet — the sinner as type). This grammar-level distinction maps onto the analytical distinction between CHAR-1 (the act) and CHAR-6 (the constituted pattern and person). The Exo 9:34 phrase "sinned yet again and *hardened his heart*" contains a distinct term for the depositional consequence: the hardening (*chazeq* — to be strong, to harden) distinguishes the act of sinning from its constitutional consequence in the inner person.

**[CHAR-7] Contagious sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-7]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes the *personal sinning act* (Qal cha.ta) from the *causative transmission* (Hiphil cha.ta) through the stem. This is the core lexical distinction in CHAR-7: every verse that includes both forms (e.g. 1Ki 14:16 — "he sinned [Qal] and made Israel to sin [Hiphil]") marks the distinction explicitly. The Qal names the leader's personal sinning (CHAR-1 domain); the Hiphil names the causative extension to the community (CHAR-7 domain). The vocabulary thus distinguishes the *act* (Qal) from the *caused act* (Hiphil) through grammatical stem differentiation within the same root.

**[CHAR-8] Political revolt** *(E)*

**[CHAR-8]** E — Within the 9-verse corpus, pa.sha is the sole vocabulary term. The distinct aspects of political revolt are encoded grammatically rather than lexically: the ongoing-state aspect (perfect — 1Ki 12:19), the specific-event aspect (wayyiqtol — 2Ki 1:1), and the constructive-consequence aspect (compound verb — 2Ki 8:20). The vocabulary does not distinguish disposition from act through different terms; it uses the same root in different grammatical configurations to encode the temporal and aspectual dimensions.

**[CHAR-9] Sinful speech** *(E)*

**[CHAR-9]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes *act* (blasfēmia noun — the specific speech-event) from *quality/disposition* (blasfēmos adjective — the person or speech characterised by the sinful-speech orientation). The adjective form applied to persons (2Ti 3:2 — "abusive") names the settled disposition rather than a single act, paralleling the distinction between CHAR-1 (act) and CHAR-6 (dispositional formation) within the sinful speech domain. The vocabulary thus encodes both the momentary act and the settled character within a single root family.

**[CHAR-10] Specialised sinful mechanisms** *(E)*

**[CHAR-10]** E — The vocabulary distinguishes *reception* (passive deleazō — Jam 1:14) from *extension* (active deleazō — 2Pe 2:14/18): the same term deployed in passive form names the enticed victim; in active form it names the enticing practitioner. This active/passive grammatical distinction encodes the key relational distinction within the enticement mechanism. The sunupokrinomai and apostasia terms are each single-aspect in this corpus (joint-performance and covenantal-departure respectively).

**[CHAR-11] Sin as universal condition** *(E)*

**[CHAR-11]** E — Yes — the multi-term vocabulary distinguishes distinct aspects of the condition. (1) *Hamartia (G0266) — the condition as power and debt*: names sin in its dominating and relational-obligation dimensions; (2) *Paraptōma (G3900) — the condition as falling-aside*: names the relational-stepping-aside dimension, the trespass-offense; (3) *Rish.ah (H7564) — the condition as settled wickedness-identity*: names the constitutive character-dimension; (4) *Chat.tat (H2403B) — the condition as crouching entity*: names the predatory-power dimension (Gen 4:7). These distinct terms are not synonymous but each names a different facet: the power/debt face (hamartia), the relational-offense face (paraptōma), the character face (rish.ah), and the predatory-entity face (chat.tat).

**[CHAR-12] Sin as enslaving power** *(E)*

**[CHAR-12]** E — The noun/verb distinction within the corpus distinguishes two aspects: (1) *Hamartia as noun-power* (Joh 8:34; Gal 3:22): sin as the governing master — the condition-aspect, naming sin's status as an entity with authority; (2) *Hamartanō as verb-practice* (1Jo 3:8/9; 5:16/18): sinning as the ongoing behavioural pattern — the act-stream aspect, naming the practice that generates and evidences the enslavement. These two aspects together constitute the characteristic: the noun-power is what the verb-practice installs and maintains.

**[CHAR-13] Sin as divine record** *(E)*

**[CHAR-13]** E — Yes. The three noun forms distinguish aspects: (1) *Chat.tat (H2403B) — the act-as-retained-fact*: sin as the thing committed that now has objective standing; (2) *Chet (H2399) — the personal-liability dimension*: sin as what the individual bears ("bear his sin" — Num 9:13); (3) *Cha.ta.ah (H2401) — the category-requiring-covering dimension*: sin as the objective moral category that needs a covering act (Psa 32:1 — "whose sin is covered"). These three noun forms, while related, distinguish sin's facthood (chat.tat), its personal-bearing (chet), and its category-status requiring concealment (cha.ta.ah).

**[CHAR-14] Forgiveness sought and received** *(E)*

**[CHAR-14]** E — Yes. The two primary term-pairs distinguish the mechanism from the object: (1) *Kip.pu.rim* names the covering-mechanism (the atonement institution and its operations); (2) *Chat.tat/hamartia/paraptōma* names the object being addressed (the sin/trespass requiring covering). Additionally: *hamartēma* (Mar 3:28/29) names individual specific sin-acts, distinguishing from hamartia's broader condition. The verb *aphiēmi* (to forgive, to release — implied in Luk 7:47/48 — "apheomai" — "are forgiven") names the divine releasing-act that accompanies the covering, complementing the noun-institutions with the verbal event of divine release.

**[CHAR-15] Generational sin** *(S)*

**[CHAR-15]** S — No. The 8-verse corpus uses only cha.ta (H2398) without companion terms that distinguish the inherited-condition dimension from the individual-act dimension. The generational transmission mechanism has no dedicated vocabulary in this corpus; it is evidenced entirely through contextual attribution (ancestral — Isa 43:27; prolonged duration — Isa 64:5) rather than through distinct terms. This is analytically significant: the inherited condition is linguistically indistinguishable from individual sinning at the term level; only context reveals the generational dimension.

**[CHAR-16] The sinner as moral character** *(E)*

**[CHAR-16]** E — Yes — the two primary terms distinguish distinct aspects. Chat.ta (H2400 — OT) emphasises the extreme-habitual-type aspect: the *qattāl* agent-noun form signals intensive/habitual sinning that has totalised the character. Hamartōlos (G0268 — NT) is broader and more inclusive: it covers social category (VCG-01), constituted identity (VCG-02), and extreme type (VCG-03 in the NT). Within hamartōlos: the adjectival use ("sinful man" — Luk 5:8; "sinful generation" — Mar 8:38) emphasises the characterising dimension; the noun use ("the sinner" — Luk 7:37; "sinners" — Mat 9:10) emphasises the identity-category dimension.

**[CHAR-17] Guilt as inner-being state** *(E)*

**[CHAR-17]** E — Yes — the vocabulary actively distinguishes the recognition-moment (a.sham verb — VCG-01), the accumulated-condition (ash.mah noun — VCG-02), the transferable-burden (a.von H5771H — VCG-03), the punitive-consequence (a.von H5771I — VCG-04), and the conscience-stagger (pu.qah — VCG-05). These are five distinct terms/senses for five distinct aspects of the same guilt-phenomenon. The vocabulary diversity within CHAR-17 is the highest of any M10 characteristic studied — five distinct term-groups for one characteristic — reflecting the guilt-state's multi-dimensional inner reality.

**[CHAR-18] Iniquity as accumulated moral crime** *(E)*

**[CHAR-18]** E — The 162-verse corpus uses a.von (H5771G) exclusively without supplementary terms that distinguish its aspects; the semantic range is carried by context and VCG structure rather than by distinct term-sets. Within individual verses, a.von is often paired with complementary terms: Exo 34:7 — "forgiving iniquity (*a.von*) and transgression (*pĕšaʿ*) and sin (*ḥaṭṭāʾt*)" — the three-term formula distinguishes iniquity (accumulated crime) from transgression (rebellious act) and sin (act of missing the mark), but CHAR-18 covers only the a.von H5771G register within this pairing.

**[CHAR-19] Transgression as deliberate boundary-crossing** *(E)*

**[CHAR-19]** E — Yes — the four term-families actively distinguish distinct aspects. (1) *Pe.sha/pa.sha* — the rebellion/breach-of-relationship register (OT); (2) *Sa.rah* — the revolt/turning-aside register (VCG-02 — inner defiance oriented against authority); (3) *Parabasis-family* — the law-violation/boundary-crossing register (NT — legally precise); (4) *Paraptōma* — the stumbling-aside/trespass register (NT — less legalistic, more moral-direction emphasis). The four families together cover: relational rebellion (pe.sha), inner defiant orientation (sa.rah), legal boundary-crossing (parabasis), and moral-path deviation (paraptōma) — four distinct angles on the same deliberate boundary-crossing reality.

**[CHAR-20] Faithlessness as covenant-breaking sin** *(E)*

**[CHAR-20]** E — Yes — the two term-families actively distinguish two aspects of the same faithlessness-reality. (1) *Ma.al* — the sacred-covenantal breach dimension: emphasises the violation of what is owed to God in the covenant or to sacred things; the hidden/covert character of the breach; (2) *Ba.gad* — the relational-betrayal dimension: emphasises the personal, interpersonal character of the treachery; the friendly-face-concealing-hostility dynamic (Jer 12:6); the constitutional settled character of the traitor (Isa 24:16; Isa 48:8). Together: ma.al names the sacred-breach; ba.gad names the relational-betrayal. Both are required to cover CHAR-20's full semantic range.

**[CHAR-21] Perversion as inner inversion** *(E)*

**[CHAR-21]** E — Yes — the nine term-families actively distinguish distinct aspects. (1) *Tah.pu.khah* — the overturned/inverted quality (speech, heart-devising); (2) *Sa.laph* — the subverting of foundational structures (judgment); (3) *A.vah* — the twisting of personal moral direction; (4) *Te.vel* — the confusion of created-order categories; (5) *Sur* — the degenerative turning-aside from original purity; (6) *Cha.val* — the destructive corruption/ruin; (7) *Ftheirō/fthora* — the progressive decay through desire. No other M10 characteristic has this term-family breadth; CHAR-21 is M10's most terminologically complex characteristic.

**[CHAR-22] Injustice as moral failure of right conduct** *(E)*

**[CHAR-22]** E — Yes — the term-families distinguish three aspects. (1) *The wrong-act aspect*: a.vel/av.lah/adikēma — the specific doing of wrong; (2) *The wrong-character aspect*: av.val/adikos — the person constituted by injustice; (3) *The wrong-condition aspect*: av.lah as a state that can "dwell in one's tents" (Job 11:14) or be "drunk like water" (Job 15:16). These three aspects (act, character, condition) are linguistically distinguished and analytically separable — CHAR-22 operates at all three levels simultaneously.

---

### T7.1.5

**Question:** Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?

**[CHAR-1] Wilful sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-1]** E — The corpus evidences the structural opposite through negative constructions rather than a dedicated antonym. "Did not sin" (lo cha.ta — Job 1:22; 2:10; 1Sa 24:11; Judg 11:27) names the opposite as the absence of the act. Eze 3:21 ("he does not sin") names the opposite as the outcome of heeding warning. The positive opposite is named in Eze 18:20 through the contrast pair: "the righteousness of the righteous shall be upon himself, and the wickedness of the wicked shall be upon himself" — righteousness as the structural opposite at the character level. Within the CHAR-1 act corpus, the structural opposite is not a single dedicated term but the absence of the sinning act (lo cha.ta) plus the presence of integrity (tummah — Gen 20:6: "integrity of heart").

**[CHAR-2] Unintentional sinning** *(E)*

**[CHAR-2]** E — The structural opposite of unintentional sinning is evidenced in the Numbers 15 context (adjacent to the CHAR-2 corpus) as *high-handed sinning* (b'yad ramah — Num 15:30, not in scope) — sinning with a raised hand of defiance, the explicit opposite of *bishgagah* (inadvertence). Within the 18-verse corpus, the structural opposite is not lexically named but is implied: the person who acts with full knowledge of the commandment and in full adherence to it — a posture unnamed by a single term but present as the assumed norm from which inadvertent sinning deviates.

**[CHAR-3] Confession** *(E)*

**[CHAR-3]** E — The structural opposite of confession within the corpus is evidenced not by a dedicated term but by the VCG-03 pattern (Deu 1:41) and the Pharaoh pattern (Exo 9:27/10:16 reversed): confession-without-following-action and confession-that-evaporates. The implied structural opposite is *silence before recognised sin* — the person who knows they sinned and does not speak. Within the broader M10 cluster, CHAR-4 (Conscience suppression) names the most direct opposite — the conscience that witnesses sin but is refused rather than voiced.
